The group claimed that they had taken not only company data but user data as well. After the breach, The Impact Team dumped emails from the company's CEO, to prove their point, and threatened to dump customer data unless the website was taken down permanently. With this initial data release, the group stated "Avid Life Media has been instructed to take Ashley Madison and Established Men offline permanently in all forms, or we will release all customer records, including profiles with all the customers' secret sexual fantasies and matching credit card transactions, real names and addresses, and employee documents and emails. The other websites may stay online."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> When Avid Life Media, the parent company that created the Ashley Madison website, did not take the site offline, The Impact Group released two more compressed files, one 9.7GB and the second 20GB. After the second data dump, Avid Life Media CEO Noel Biderman resigned, but the website remained functional.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues_and_global_regulation">Legal issues and global regulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Legal issues and global regulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Conflict of laws in cyberspace has become a major cause of concern for computer security community. Some of the main challenges and complaints about the antivirus industry are the lack of global web regulations, a global base of common rules to judge, and eventually punish, <a href="/wiki/Cybercrime" title="Cybercrime">cyber crimes</a> and cyber criminals. There is no global cyber law and cybersecurity treaty that can be invoked for enforcing global cybersecurity issues.</p>
<p>International legal issues of cyber attacks are complicated in nature. Even if an antivirus firm locates the cyber criminal behind the creation of a particular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virus_(computer)" title="Virus (computer)">virus</a> or piece of <a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">malware</a> or form of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyber-Attacks" title="Cyber-Attacks">cyber attack</a>, often the local authorities cannot take action due to lack of laws under which to prosecute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ted.com_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-ted.com-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Authorship attribution for cyber crimes and cyber attacks is a major problem for all law enforcement agencies.</p>
<p>"[Computer viruses] switch from one country to another, from one jurisdiction to another – moving around the world, using the fact that we don't have the capability to globally police operations like this. So the Internet is as if someone [had] given free plane tickets to all the online criminals of the world."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ted.com_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-ted.com-106">[106]</a></sup> Use of <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_DNS" title="Dynamic DNS">dynamic DNS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fast_flux" title="Fast flux">fast flux</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulletproof_hosting" title="Bulletproof hosting">bullet proof servers</a> have added own complexities to this situation.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_2">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The role of the government is to make <a href="/wiki/Cyber-security_regulation" title="Cyber-security regulation">regulations</a> to force companies and organizations to protect their systems, infrastructure and information from any <a href="/wiki/Cyber-attack" title="Cyber-attack">cyber-attacks</a>, but also to protect its own national infrastructure such as the national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_grid" title="Power grid">power-grid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>The question of whether the government should intervene or not in the regulation of the <a href="/wiki/Cyberspace" title="Cyberspace">cyberspace</a> is a very polemical one. Indeed, for as long as it has existed and by definition, the cyberspace is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virtual_space" title="Virtual space">virtual space</a> free of any government intervention. Where everyone agree that an improvement on cybersecurity is more than vital, is the government the best actor to solve this issue? Many government officials and experts think that the government should step in and that there is a crucial need for regulation, mainly due to the failure of the private sector to solve efficiently the cybersecurity problem. <a href="/wiki/Richard_A._Clarke" title="Richard A. Clarke">R. Clarke</a> said during a panel discussion at the <a href="/wiki/RSA_Conference" title="RSA Conference">RSA Security Conference</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, he believes that the "industry only responds when you threaten regulation. If industry doesn't respond (to the threat), you have to follow through."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarke_ref_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clarke_ref-109">[109]</a></sup> On the other hand, executives from the private sector agree that improvements are necessary, but think that the government intervention would affect their ability to innovate efficiently.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Actions_and_teams_in_the_US">Actions and teams in the US</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Actions and teams in the US">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislation">Legislation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Legislation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1986 <a href="/wiki/Title_18_of_the_United_States_Code" title="Title 18 of the United States Code">18 U.S.C.</a> <a class="external text" href="https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/18/1030" rel="nofollow">§ 1030</a>, more commonly known as the <a href="/wiki/Computer_Fraud_and_Abuse_Act" title="Computer Fraud and Abuse Act">Computer Fraud and Abuse Act</a> is the key legislation. It prohibits unauthorized access or damage of "protected computers" as defined in <span class="plainlinksneverexpand"><a href="/wiki/Title_18_of_the_United_States_Code" title="Title 18 of the United States Code">18 U.S.C.</a> <a class="external text" href="https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/18/1030#e_2" rel="nofollow">§ 1030(e)(2)</a></span>.</p>
<p>Although various other measures have been proposed, such as the "Cybersecurity Act of 2010 – S. 773" in 2009, the "International Cybercrime Reporting and Cooperation Act – H.R.4962"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> and "Protecting Cyberspace as a National Asset Act of 2010 – S.3480"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> in 2010 – none of these has succeeded.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Executive_order" title="Executive order">Executive order</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Executive_Order_13636" title="wikisource:Executive Order 13636">13636</a> <i>Improving Critical Infrastructure Cybersecurity</i> was signed February 12, 2013.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agencies">Agencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Agencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a> has a dedicated division responsible for the response system, <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">risk management</a> program and requirements for cybersecurity in the United States called the <a href="/wiki/National_Cyber_Security_Division" title="National Cyber Security Division">National Cyber Security Division</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSRDC-FAQ_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-CSRDC-FAQ-113">[113]</a></sup> The division is home to US-CERT operations and the National Cyber Alert System.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSRDC-FAQ_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-CSRDC-FAQ-113">[113]</a></sup> The National Cybersecurity and Communications Integration Center brings together government organizations responsible for protecting computer networks and networked infrastructure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>The third priority of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> (FBI) is to: <i>"Protect the United States against cyber-based attacks and high-technology crimes"</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-priorities_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-priorities-115">[115]</a></sup> and they, along with the <a href="/wiki/National_White_Collar_Crime_Center" title="National White Collar Crime Center">National White Collar Crime Center</a> (NW3C), and the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Justice_Assistance" title="Bureau of Justice Assistance">Bureau of Justice Assistance</a> (BJA) are part of the multi-agency task force, The <a href="/wiki/Internet_Crime_Complaint_Center" title="Internet Crime Complaint Center">Internet Crime Complaint Center</a>, also known as IC3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ic3_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-ic3-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to its own specific duties, the FBI participates alongside non-profit organizations such as <a href="/wiki/InfraGard" title="InfraGard">InfraGard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-infragard-site_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-infragard-site-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mueller-video_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-mueller-video-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice_Criminal_Division" title="United States Department of Justice Criminal Division">criminal division</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> operates a section called the <a href="/wiki/Computer_Crime_and_Intellectual_Property_Section" title="Computer Crime and Intellectual Property Section">Computer Crime and Intellectual Property Section</a>. The CCIPS is in charge of investigating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_crime" title="Computer crime">computer crime</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_property" title="Intellectual property">intellectual property</a> crime and is specialized in the search and seizure of <a href="/wiki/Digital_evidence" title="Digital evidence">digital evidence</a> in computers and <a href="/wiki/Computer_network" title="Computer network">networks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CCIPS_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-CCIPS-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USCYBERCOM" title="USCYBERCOM">United States Cyber Command</a>, also known as USCYBERCOM, is tasked with the defense of specified Department of Defense information networks and <i>"ensure US/Allied freedom of action in cyberspace and deny the same to our adversaries."</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> It has no role in the protection of civilian networks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a>'s role in cybersecurity is to strengthen the protection of critical communications infrastructure, to assist in maintaining the reliability of networks during disasters, to aid in swift recovery after, and to ensure that first responders have access to effective communications services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCC_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FCC-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> has issued guidance for medical devices,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> is concerned with automotive cybersecurity. After being criticized by the <a href="/wiki/Government_Accountability_Office" title="Government Accountability Office">Government Accountability Office</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> and following successful attacks on airports and claimed attacks on airplanes, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a> has devoted funding to securing systems on board the planes of private manufacturers, and the <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_Communications_Addressing_and_Reporting_System" title="Aircraft Communications Addressing and Reporting System">Aircraft Communications Addressing and Reporting System</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Concerns have also been raised about the future <a href="/wiki/Next_Generation_Air_Transportation_System" title="Next Generation Air Transportation System">Next Generation Air Transportation System</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer_emergency_readiness_team">Computer emergency readiness team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Computer emergency readiness team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Computer_emergency_response_team" title="Computer emergency response team">Computer emergency response team</a>" is a name given to expert groups that handle computer security incidents. In the US, two distinct organization exist, although they do work closely together.</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US-CERT" title="US-CERT">US-CERT</a>: part of the <a href="/wiki/National_Cyber_Security_Division" title="National Cyber Security Division">National Cyber Security Division</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">United States Department of Homeland Security</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Computerworld_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Computerworld-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CERT_Coordination_Center" title="CERT Coordination Center">CERT/CC</a>: created by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Defense_Advanced_Research_Projects_Agency" title="Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency">Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency</a> (DARPA) and run by the <a href="/wiki/Software_Engineering_Institute" title="Software Engineering Institute">Software Engineering Institute</a> (SEI).</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_actions">International actions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: International actions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Many different teams and organisations exist, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>The Forum of Incident Response and Security Teams (FIRST) is the global association of CSIRTs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIRST_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIRST-130">[130]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US-CERT" title="US-CERT">US-CERT</a>, <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cisco" title="Cisco">Cisco</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McAfee" title="McAfee">McAfee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> are all members of this international team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIRST_members_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIRST_members-131">[131]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> helps protect societies worldwide from the threat of cybercrime through the Convention on Cybercrime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_council_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-European_council-132">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li>The purpose of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Messaging_Anti-Abuse_Working_Group" title="Messaging Anti-Abuse Working Group">Messaging Anti-Abuse Working Group</a> (MAAWG) is to bring the messaging industry together to work collaboratively and to successfully address the various forms of messaging abuse, such as spam, viruses, denial-of-service attacks and other messaging exploitations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MAAWG_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-MAAWG-133">[133]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/France_T%C3%A9l%C3%A9com" title="France Télécom">France Telecom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cisco" title="Cisco">Cisco</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sprint_Nextel" title="Sprint Nextel">Sprint</a> are some of the members of the MAAWG.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MAAWGroster_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-MAAWGroster-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li>ENISA : The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Network_and_Information_Security_Agency" title="European Network and Information Security Agency">European Network and Information Security Agency</a> (ENISA) is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agency_of_the_European_Union" title="Agency of the European Union">agency of the European Union</a> with the objective to improve network and <a href="/wiki/Information_security" title="Information security">information security</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>CSIRTs in Europe collaborate in the <a href="/wiki/TERENA" title="TERENA">TERENA</a> task force TF-CSIRT. <a href="/wiki/TERENA" title="TERENA">TERENA</a>'s Trusted Introducer service provides an accreditation and certification scheme for CSIRTs in Europe. A full list of known CSIRTs in Europe is available from the Trusted Introducer website.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_teams">National teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: National teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Here are the main <a href="/wiki/Computer_emergency_response_team" title="Computer emergency response team">computer emergency response teams</a> around the world. Most countries have their own team to protect network security.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On October 3, 2010, Public Safety Canada unveiled Canada's Cyber Security Strategy, following a Speech from the Throne commitment to boost the security of Canadian cyberspace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canada.27s_Cyber_Security_Strategy_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Canada.27s_Cyber_Security_Strategy-136">[136]</a></sup> The aim of the strategy is to strengthen Canada's "cyber systems and critical infrastructure sectors, support economic growth and protect Canadians as they connect to each other and to the world."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canada.27s_Cyber_Security_Strategy_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-Canada.27s_Cyber_Security_Strategy-136">[136]</a></sup> Three main pillars define the strategy: securing government systems, partnering to secure vital cyber systems outside the federal government, and helping Canadians to be secure online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canada.27s_Cyber_Security_Strategy_136-2"><a href="#cite_note-Canada.27s_Cyber_Security_Strategy-136">[136]</a></sup> The strategy involves multiple departments and agencies across the Government of Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Government_of_Canada_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Government_of_Canada-137">[137]</a></sup> The Cyber Incident Management Framework for Canada outlines these responsibilities, and provides a plan for coordinated response between government and other partners in the event of a cyber incident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The Action Plan 2010–2015 for Canada's Cyber Security Strategy outlines the ongoing implementation of the strategy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Public Safety Canada's <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Cyber_Incident_Response_Centre" title="Canadian Cyber Incident Response Centre">Canadian Cyber Incident Response Centre</a> (CCIRC) is responsible for mitigating and responding to threats to Canada's critical infrastructure and cyber systems. The CCIRC provides support to mitigate cyber threats, technical support to respond and recover from targeted cyber attacks, and provides online tools for members of Canada's critical infrastructure sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The CCIRC posts regular cyber security bulletins on the Public Safety Canada website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The CCIRC also operates an online reporting tool where individuals and organizations can report a cyber incident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Canada's Cyber Security Strategy is part of a larger, integrated approach to critical infrastructure protection, and functions as a counterpart document to the National Strategy and Action Plan for Critical Infrastructure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Government_of_Canada_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-Government_of_Canada-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 27, 2010, Public Safety Canada partnered with STOP.THINK.CONNECT, a coalition of non-profit, private sector, and government organizations dedicated to informing the general public on how to protect themselves online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> On February 4, 2014, the Government of Canada launched the Cyber Security Cooperation Program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The program is a $1.5 million five-year initiative aimed at improving Canada's cyber systems through grants and contributions to projects in support of this objective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Public Safety Canada aims to begin an evaluation of Canada's Cyber Security Strategy in early 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Government_of_Canada_137-2"><a href="#cite_note-Government_of_Canada-137">[137]</a></sup> Public Safety Canada administers and routinely updates the GetCyberSafe portal for Canadian citizens, and carries out Cyber Security Awareness Month during October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>China's network security and information technology leadership team was established February 27, 2014. The leadership team is tasked with national security and long-term development and co-ordination of major issues related to network security and information technology. Economic, political, cultural, social and military fields as related to network security and information technology strategy, planning and major macroeconomic policy are being researched. The promotion of national network security and information technology law are constantly under study for enhanced national security capabilities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Berlin starts National Cyber Defense Initiative: On June 16, 2011, the German Minister for Home Affairs, officially opened the new German NCAZ (National Center for Cyber Defense) <a href="/wiki/National_Cyberdefence_Centre" title="National Cyberdefence Centre">Nationales Cyber-Abwehrzentrum</a> located in Bonn. The NCAZ closely cooperates with BSI (Federal Office for Information Security) <a href="/wiki/Federal_Office_for_Information_Security" title="Federal Office for Information Security">Bundesamt für Sicherheit in der Informationstechnik</a>, BKA (Federal Police Organisation) <a href="/wiki/Federal_Criminal_Police_Office_(Germany)" title="Federal Criminal Police Office (Germany)">Bundeskriminalamt (Deutschland)</a>, BND (Federal Intelligence Service) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bundesnachrichtendienst" title="Bundesnachrichtendienst">Bundesnachrichtendienst</a>, MAD (Military Intelligence Service) <a href="/wiki/Milit%C3%A4rischer_Abschirmdienst" title="Militärischer Abschirmdienst">Amt für den Militärischen Abschirmdienst</a> and other national organisations in Germany taking care of national security aspects. According to the Minister the primary task of the new organisation founded on February 23, 2011, is to detect and prevent attacks against the national infrastructure and mentioned incidents like <a href="/wiki/Stuxnet" title="Stuxnet">Stuxnet</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some provisions for cybersecurity have been incorporated into rules framed under the Information Technology Act 2000.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Cyber_Security_Policy_2013" title="National Cyber Security Policy 2013">National Cyber Security Policy 2013</a> is a policy framework by Department of Electronics and Information Technology (DeitY) which aims to protect the public and private infrastructure from cyber attacks, and safeguard "information, such as personal information (of web users), financial and banking information and sovereign data".</p>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Indian_Companies_Act_2013&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Indian Companies Act 2013 (page does not exist)">Indian Companies Act 2013</a> has also introduced cyber law and cyber security obligations on the part of Indian directors.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cyber-crime has risen rapidly in Pakistan. There are about 30 million Internet users with 15 million mobile subscribers in Pakistan. According to Cyber Crime Unit (CCU), a branch of Federal Investigation Agency, only 62 cases were reported to the unit in 2007, 287 cases in 2008, ratio dropped in 2009 but in 2010, more than 312 cases were registered. However, there are many unreported incidents of cyber-crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tier3_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tier3-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Pakistan's Cyber Crime Bill 2007", the first pertinent law, focuses on electronic crimes, for example cyber-terrorism, criminal access, electronic system fraud, electronic forgery, and misuse of encryption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tier3_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tier3-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>National Response Centre for Cyber Crime (NR3C) – FIA is a law enforcement agency dedicated to fight cybercrime. Inception of this Hi-Tech crime fighting unit transpired in 2007 to identify and curb the phenomenon of technological abuse in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> However, certain private firms are also working in cohesion with the government to improve cyber security and curb cyberattacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Korea">South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: South Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following cyberattacks in the first half of 2013, when government, news-media, television station, and bank websites were compromised, the national government committed to the training of 5,000 new cybersecurity experts by 2017. The South Korean government blamed its northern counterpart for these attacks, as well as incidents that occurred in 2009, 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-South_Korean_news_agency_Yonhap_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-South_Korean_news_agency_Yonhap-150">[150]</a></sup> and 2012, but Pyongyang denies the accusations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jun_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jun-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_countries">Other countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Other countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>CERT <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, member of FIRST (Forum for Incident Response and Security Teams)</li>
<li>CARNet CERT, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, member of FIRST</li>
<li>AE CERT, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a></li>
<li>SingCERT, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a></li>
<li>CERT-LEXSI, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a></li>
<li>INCIBE, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_warfare">Modern warfare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Modern warfare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare" title="Cyberwarfare">Cyberwarfare</a></div>
<p>Cybersecurity is becoming increasingly important as more information and technology is being made available on cyberspace. There is growing concern among governments that cyberspace will become the next theatre of warfare. As Mark Clayton from the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_Science_Monitor" title="Christian Science Monitor">Christian Science Monitor</a></i> described in an article titled "The New Cyber Arms Race":</p>
<blockquote>
<p>In the future, wars will not just be fought by soldiers with guns or with planes that drop bombs. They will also be fought with the click of a mouse a half a world away that unleashes carefully weaponized computer programs that disrupt or destroy critical industries like utilities, transportation, communications, and energy. Such attacks could also disable military networks that control the movement of troops, the path of jet fighters, the command and control of warships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_new_cyber_arms_race_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_new_cyber_arms_race-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>This has led to new terms such as <i><a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare" title="Cyberwarfare">cyberwarfare</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Cyberterrorism" title="Cyberterrorism">cyberterrorism</a></i>. More and more critical infrastructure is being controlled via computer programs that, while increasing efficiency, exposes new vulnerabilities. The test will be to see if governments and corporations that control critical systems such as energy, communications and other information will be able to prevent attacks before they occur. As Jay Cross, the chief scientist of the Internet Time Group, remarked, "Connectedness begets vulnerability."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_new_cyber_arms_race_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_new_cyber_arms_race-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Job_market">Job market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Job market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cybersecurity is a fast-growing<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> field of <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">IT</a> concerned with reducing organizations' risk of hack or data breach. According to research from the Enterprise Strategy Group, 46% of organizations say that they have a "problematic shortage" of cybersecurity skills in 2016, up from 28% in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Commercial, government and non-governmental organizations all employ cybersecurity professionals. The fastest increases in demand for cybersecurity workers are in industries managing increasing volumes of consumer data such as finance, health care, and retail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> However, the use of the term "cybersecurity" is more prevalent in government job descriptions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>Typical cybersecurity job titles and descriptions include:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Security analyst</dt>
<dd>Analyzes and assesses vulnerabilities in the infrastructure (software, hardware, networks), investigates using available tools and countermeasures to remedy the detected vulnerabilities, and recommends solutions and best practices. Analyzes and assesses damage to the data/infrastructure as a result of security incidents, examines available recovery tools and processes, and recommends solutions. Tests for compliance with security policies and procedures. May assist in the creation, implementation, and/or management of security solutions.</dd>
<dt>Security engineer</dt>
<dd>Performs security monitoring, security and data/logs analysis, and forensic analysis, to detect security incidents, and mounts incident response. Investigates and utilizes new technologies and processes to enhance security capabilities and implement improvements. May also review code or perform other <a href="/wiki/Security_engineering" title="Security engineering">security engineering</a> methodologies.</dd>
<dt>Security architect</dt>
<dd>Designs a security system or major components of a security system, and may head a security design team building a new security system.</dd>
<dt>Security administrator</dt>
<dd>Installs and manages organization-wide security systems. May also take on some of the tasks of a security analyst in smaller organizations.</dd>
<dt>Chief Information Security Officer (CISO)</dt>
<dd>A high-level management position responsible for the entire information security division/staff. The position may include hands-on technical work.</dd>
<dt>Chief Security Officer (CSO)</dt>
<dd>A high-level management position responsible for the entire security division/staff. A newer position now deemed needed as security risks grow.</dd>
<dt>Security Consultant/Specialist/Intelligence</dt>
<dd>Broad titles that encompass any one or all of the other roles/titles, tasked with protecting computers, networks, software, data, and/or information systems against viruses, worms, spyware, malware, intrusion detection, unauthorized access, denial-of-service attacks, and an ever increasing list of attacks by hackers acting as individuals or as part of organized crime or foreign governments.</dd>
</dl>
<p>Student programs are also available to people interested in beginning a career in cybersecurity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Meanwhile, a flexible and effective option for <a href="/wiki/Information_security" title="Information security">information security</a> professionals of all experience levels to keep studying is online security training, including webcasts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following terms used with regards to engineering secure systems are explained below.</p>
<ul>
<li>Access <a href="/wiki/Authorization" title="Authorization">authorization</a> restricts access to a computer to group of users through the use of <a href="/wiki/Authentication" title="Authentication">authentication</a> systems. These systems can protect either the whole computer – such as through an interactive <a href="/wiki/Login" title="Login">login</a> screen – or individual services, such as an <a href="/wiki/File_Transfer_Protocol" title="File Transfer Protocol">FTP</a> server. There are many methods for identifying and authenticating users, such as <a href="/wiki/Password" title="Password">passwords</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Identification_card" title="Identification card">identification cards</a>, and, more recently, <a href="/wiki/Smart_card" title="Smart card">smart cards</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biometric" title="Biometric">biometric</a> systems.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-virus_software" title="Anti-virus software">Anti-virus software</a> consists of computer programs that attempt to identify, thwart and eliminate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_viruses" title="Computer viruses">computer viruses</a> and other malicious software (<a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">malware</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Application_software" title="Application software">Applications</a> with known security flaws should not be run. Either leave it turned off until it can be patched or otherwise fixed, or delete it and replace it with some other application. Publicly known flaws are the main entry used by <a href="/wiki/Computer_worm" title="Computer worm">worms</a> to automatically break into a system and then spread to other systems connected to it. The security website <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secunia" title="Secunia">Secunia</a> provides a search tool for unpatched known flaws in popular products.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Authentication" title="Authentication">Authentication</a> techniques can be used to ensure that communication end-points are who they say they are.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Automated_theorem_proving" title="Automated theorem proving">Automated theorem proving</a> and other verification tools can enable critical algorithms and code used in secure systems to be mathematically proven to meet their specifications.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Backup" title="Backup">Backups</a> are a way of securing information; they are another copy of all the important computer files kept in another location. These files are kept on hard disks, <a href="/wiki/CD-R" title="CD-R">CD-Rs</a>, <a href="/wiki/CD-RW" title="CD-RW">CD-RWs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_tape_data_storage" title="Magnetic tape data storage">tapes</a> and more recently on the cloud. Suggested locations for backups are a fireproof, waterproof, and heat proof safe, or in a separate, offsite location than that in which the original files are contained. Some individuals and companies also keep their backups in <a href="/wiki/Safe_deposit_box" title="Safe deposit box">safe deposit boxes</a> inside <a href="/wiki/Bank_vault" title="Bank vault">bank vaults</a>. There is also a fourth option, which involves using one of the <a href="/wiki/File_hosting_service" title="File hosting service">file hosting services</a> that backs up files over the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> for both business and individuals, known as the cloud.
<ul>
<li>Backups are also important for reasons other than security. Natural disasters, such as earthquakes, hurricanes, or tornadoes, may strike the building where the computer is located. The building can be on fire, or an explosion may occur. There needs to be a recent backup at an alternate secure location, in case of such kind of disaster. Further, it is recommended that the alternate location be placed where the same disaster would not affect both locations. Examples of alternate disaster recovery sites being compromised by the same disaster that affected the primary site include having had a primary site in <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973%E2%80%932001)" title="World Trade Center (1973–2001)">World Trade Center</a> I and the recovery site in <a href="/wiki/7_World_Trade_Center" title="7 World Trade Center">7 World Trade Center</a>, both of which were destroyed in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/9/11" title="9/11">9/11</a> attack, and having one's primary site and recovery site in the same coastal region, which leads to both being vulnerable to hurricane damage (for example, primary site in New Orleans and recovery site in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jefferson_Parish" title="Jefferson Parish">Jefferson Parish</a>, both of which were hit by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> in 2005). The backup media should be moved between the geographic sites in a secure manner, in order to prevent them from being stolen.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capability_(computers)" title="Capability (computers)">Capability</a> and <a href="/wiki/Access_control_list" title="Access control list">access control list</a> techniques can be used to ensure privilege separation and mandatory access control. <a href="/wiki/Computer_security#Capabilities_vs._ACLs" title="Computer security">This section</a> discusses their use.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chain_of_trust" title="Chain of trust">Chain of trust</a> techniques can be used to attempt to ensure that all software loaded has been certified as authentic by the system's designers.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Confidentiality" title="Confidentiality">Confidentiality</a> is the nondisclosure of information except to another authorized person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cryptography" title="Cryptography">Cryptographic</a> techniques can be used to defend data in transit between systems, reducing the probability that data exchanged between systems can be intercepted or modified.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare" title="Cyberwarfare">Cyberwarfare</a> is an internet-based conflict that involves politically motivated attacks on information and information systems. Such attacks can, for example, disable official websites and networks, disrupt or disable essential services, steal or alter classified data, and cripple financial systems.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Data_integrity" title="Data integrity">Data integrity</a> is the accuracy and consistency of stored data, indicated by an absence of any alteration in data between two updates of a data record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Encryption_-_decryption.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1800" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Encryption_-_decryption.svg/300px-Encryption_-_decryption.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Encryption_-_decryption.svg/450px-Encryption_-_decryption.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Encryption_-_decryption.svg/600px-Encryption_-_decryption.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Encryption_-_decryption.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cryptography" title="Cryptography">Cryptographic</a> techniques involve transforming information, scrambling it so it becomes unreadable during transmission. The intended recipient can unscramble the message; ideally, eavesdroppers cannot.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Encryption" title="Encryption">Encryption</a> is used to protect the message from the eyes of others. <a href="/wiki/Cryptography" title="Cryptography">Cryptographically</a> secure <a href="/wiki/Cipher" title="Cipher">ciphers</a> are designed to make any practical attempt of <a href="/wiki/Cryptanalysis" title="Cryptanalysis">breaking</a> infeasible. <a href="/wiki/Symmetric-key_algorithm" title="Symmetric-key algorithm">Symmetric-key</a> ciphers are suitable for bulk encryption using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shared_key" title="Shared key">shared keys</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public-key_encryption" title="Public-key encryption">public-key encryption</a> using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_certificate" title="Digital certificate">digital certificates</a> can provide a practical solution for the problem of securely communicating when no key is shared in advance.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Endpoint_security" title="Endpoint security">Endpoint security</a> software helps networks to prevent exfiltration (data theft) and virus infection at network entry points made vulnerable by the prevalence of potentially infected portable computing devices, such as laptops and mobile devices, and external storage devices, such as USB drives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Firewall_(networking)" title="Firewall (networking)">Firewalls</a> are an important method for control and security on the Internet and other networks. A network firewall can be a communications processor, typically a router, or a dedicated server, along with firewall software. A firewall serves as a gatekeeper system that protects a company's intranets and other computer networks from intrusion by providing a filter and safe transfer point for access to and from the Internet and other networks. It screens all network traffic for proper passwords or other security codes and only allows authorized transmission in and out of the network. Firewalls can deter, but not completely prevent, unauthorized access (hacking) into computer networks; they can also provide some protection from online intrusion.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Honeypot_(computing)" title="Honeypot (computing)">Honey pots</a> are computers that are either intentionally or unintentionally left vulnerable to attack by crackers. They can be used to catch crackers or fix vulnerabilities.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intrusion-detection_system" title="Intrusion-detection system">Intrusion-detection systems</a> can scan a network for people that are on the network but who should not be there or are doing things that they should not be doing, for example trying a lot of passwords to gain access to the network.</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Microkernel" title="Microkernel">microkernel</a> is the near-minimum amount of software that can provide the mechanisms to implement an operating system. It is used solely to provide very low-level, very precisely defined machine code upon which an operating system can be developed. A simple example is the early '90s GEMSOS (Gemini Computers), which provided extremely low-level machine code, such as "segment" management, atop which an operating system could be built. The theory (in the case of "segments") was that—rather than have the operating system itself worry about mandatory access separation by means of military-style labeling—it is safer if a low-level, independently scrutinized module can be charged <b>solely</b> with the management of individually labeled segments, be they memory "segments" or file system "segments" or executable text "segments." If software below the visibility of the operating system is (as in this case) charged with labeling, there is no theoretically viable means for a clever hacker to subvert the labeling scheme, since the operating system <i>per se</i> does <b>not</b> provide mechanisms for interfering with labeling: the operating system is, essentially, a client (an "application," arguably) atop the microkernel and, as such, subject to its restrictions.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ping_(networking_utility)" title="Ping (networking utility)">Pinging</a> The ping application can be used by potential crackers to find if an IP address is reachable. If a cracker finds a computer, they can try a port scan to detect and attack services on that computer.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_engineering_(computer_security)" title="Social engineering (computer security)">Social engineering</a> awareness keeps employees aware of the dangers of social engineering and/or having a policy in place to prevent social engineering can reduce successful breaches of the network and servers.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Computer_security&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><cite class="citation book">Wu, Chwan-Hwa (John); Irwin, J. David (2013). <i>Introduction to Computer Networks and Cybersecurity</i>.
